## Section 001: Kotlin Backend Testing Fixtures
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Testing Fixtures", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title names testing fixtures but does not yet expose the governing choice between a cheap boundary-focused proof and a broader integration proof
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Testing Fixtures", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a narrow proof shortens feedback while a deliberately realistic dependency prevents an in-memory substitute from producing false confidence about dialects, transactions, cancellation, or protocol behavior
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Testing Fixtures", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the test double omits the behavior being claimed, full startup is used without a cross-layer reason, or a passing happy path is treated as proof of cancellation, rollback, authorization, or production-dialect semantics
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Testing Fixtures", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply this reference within an existing Kotlin backend and preserve its framework, build wrapper, test framework, database dialect, and CI constraints unless repository evidence authorizes a change
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Testing Fixtures", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to turn the opening into a boundary-to-proof contract that names escalation triggers, counterexamples, fixture ownership, and observable pass or stop conditions
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Testing Fixtures", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that fixture realism should be allocated by semantic risk rather than by layer prestige, so a five-line domain test can be stronger than a full startup test while one database container can be indispensable
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Testing Fixtures", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: the test double omits the behavior being claimed, full startup is used without a cross-layer reason, or a passing happy path is treated as proof of cancellation, rollback, authorization, or production-dialect semantics

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Testing Fixtures", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where the requirement has an identifiable transport, domain, persistence, coroutine, integration, or migration risk and the repository already exposes a test harness for that boundary

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed accurately lists one local testing guide and four public Kotlin ecosystem pointers, but the rows do not say which testing claim each source may govern, whether it was refreshed, or when repository behavior must override a generic example
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a source can be authoritative for language syntax yet irrelevant to a Spring slice, or authoritative for Ktor test hosting yet silent about a project's transaction adapter
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: URL presence is mistaken for reviewed evidence, a Spring sample is generalized to Ktor, coroutine library behavior is inferred from memory, or the single local guide is treated as proof of every repository-specific fixture
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: do not infer freshness from an external URL, do not transfer framework-specific advice across Spring and Ktor, and keep observed repository behavior distinct from archived policy and unrefreshed public pointers
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain every seed row while adding claim scope, framework match, retrieval state, repository corroboration, and explicit invalidation criteria
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that with only one local policy document, executable repository evidence becomes the decisive corroboration layer; it narrows application without silently becoming a second canonical prose source

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed records three reference-generation failures, but a testing-fixtures guide also needs concrete backend test smells that can pass review while failing to expose production behavior
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because these smells either hide the behavior under claim or add unrelated state and timing, producing suites that are simultaneously slow and weak
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the registry becomes a style blacklist, forbids mocks or full startup categorically, or flags a smell without considering whether the dependency behavior is actually part of the requirement
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply registry findings to the claim and boundary under review, preserving justified exceptions with executable evidence rather than blanket waivers
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to keep the original provenance rows and add Kotlin-specific detection, exception, recovery, and fault-injection criteria
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that anti-pattern severity is proportional to false-negative risk, not aesthetic dislike; a slow test is tolerable if uniquely probative, while a fast mock test is harmful if it erases the disputed semantics
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to retain the three provenance safeguards and add boundary-specific checks for overbroad startup, excessive mocking, production-dialect substitution, real sleeps, shared mutable fixtures, happy-path-only contracts, and nondeterministic data

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the registry becomes a style blacklist, forbids mocks or full startup categorically, or flags a smell without considering whether the dependency behavior is actually part of the requirement
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: apply registry findings to the claim and boundary under review, preserving justified exceptions with executable evidence rather than blanket waivers
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: keep the original provenance rows and add Kotlin-specific detection, exception, recovery, and fault-injection criteria
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies anti-pattern severity is proportional to false-negative risk, not aesthetic dislike; a slow test is tolerable if uniquely probative, while a fast mock test is harmful if it erases the disputed semantics

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed provides the archived reference-generation verifier, which can validate the document pipeline but cannot prove any Kotlin test, fixture, database, coroutine, or framework behavior
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because artifact correctness and backend behavior are independent failure surfaces; one command cannot substitute for the other
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the archive generator command is presented as a service test, a missing wrapper is silently replaced by a global tool, a filtered test is the only final evidence, or flaky reruns are counted as success
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: never claim an unconfigured or unexecuted command passed, never use a global build tool when the wrapper is authoritative, and scope performance or infrastructure claims to the environment actually measured
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain the original generation command while separating artifact, focused behavior, full repository, lint, and unavailable-gate outcomes
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a trustworthy gate packet is layered: document structure proves the reference is usable, focused tests prove the change mechanism, and the full build protects integration; dropping a layer narrows the claim

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed says when to open the reference and to preserve evidence labels, but it does not give an agent a deterministic path from requirement risk to test type, fixture scope, and escalation
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because sequencing prevents a tool or fixture preference from preceding the behavior that must be proven and preserves causal evidence through the implementation loop
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the task is primarily production operations or security policy, no target behavior is specified, the required real dependency is unavailable, or the agent begins by generating generic tests from class names
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this guide for test-design and fixture decisions within an existing Kotlin backend, not as authority to redesign the framework, production topology, or security model
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to convert the seed bullets into an inspect-select-Red-implement-verify-escalate workflow with explicit stop and routing conditions
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that agent autonomy is safest when bounded by stop conditions: inability to name the failure, harness, or evidence is a reason to pause and inspect, not a reason to generate more test code

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed names a Kotlin backend builder and a broad production-safety goal, but it does not carry that user through a concrete fixture decision, evidence conflict, or completion signal
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the maintainer needs a navigable path from risk to proof; broad production-safety language cannot choose between a unit test, framework slice, real database, virtual clock, or simulated external peer
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the request is only 'add tests', ownership is unclear, the desired behavior conflicts with existing contracts, or required infrastructure and credentials cannot be safely obtained
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: assume maintenance of one existing Kotlin backend capability and do not infer permission to migrate frameworks, access production data, or provision shared infrastructure
- **revision_decision:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to expand the opening scenario into requirement discovery, boundary mapping, fixture choice, evidence conflict, verification, and escalation stages
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a useful journey ends with a decision artifact and a stop condition, not merely a passing test; unresolved realism gaps must remain visible to the next reviewer
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to begin with the user's observable outcome and likely failure, trace it to transport, domain, persistence, coroutine, or integration boundaries, inventory the existing harness, and build a verification matrix before touching production implementation

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed supplies Adopt, Adapt, Avoid, and Cost of being wrong rows, but its conditions remain source-oriented and do not compare feedback speed, semantic fidelity, isolation, setup cost, and diagnostic precision across test choices
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because test strategy is an economic choice among detection power, execution cost, maintenance burden, and consequence of a missed defect
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: Adopt becomes automatic compliance, Adapt quietly weakens the assertion, Avoid means no verification, or cost-of-being-wrong language inflates ordinary low-risk code into a production incident
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: compare only viable choices for the existing framework and CI environment, and keep high-consequence escalation proportional to actual user and system impact
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to make each inherited decision row evaluate fixture fidelity, feedback economics, failure consequence, and an explicit evidence-producing action
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that hybrid portfolios usually dominate single-test-type policies because cheap tests protect invariants while a few realistic tests guard semantic discontinuities such as dialects, transactions, and framework wiring
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to adopt when the breakable boundary and existing harness are clear, adapt when realism or framework constraints differ, avoid when no behavior can be stated or observed, and escalate when an incorrect test would authorize destructive migration, security, money, or concurrency behavior
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because test strategy is an economic choice among detection power, execution cost, maintenance burden, and consequence of a missed defect
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; Adopt becomes automatic compliance, Adapt quietly weakens the assertion, Avoid means no verification, or cost-of-being-wrong language inflates ordinary low-risk code into a production incident
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: compare only viable choices for the existing framework and CI environment, and keep high-consequence escalation proportional to actual user and system impact
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: make each inherited decision row evaluate fixture fidelity, feedback economics, failure consequence, and an explicit evidence-producing action
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies hybrid portfolios usually dominate single-test-type policies because cheap tests protect invariants while a few realistic tests guard semantic discontinuities such as dialects, transactions, and framework wiring
### Question 03: When does the default work well?

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: Adopt becomes automatic compliance, Adapt quietly weakens the assertion, Avoid means no verification, or cost-of-being-wrong language inflates ordinary low-risk code into a production incident

## Section 012: Local Corpus Hierarchy
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed labels the sole local testing guide canonical and warns that one mapped source is insufficient for organization-wide policy, but it does not define how supporting repository evidence differs from additional corpus authority
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because authority, recency, and executability are different properties; a running legacy test may be current but still encode an obsolete policy, while a canonical guide may be authoritative but intentionally generic
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: generated references are counted as new canonical sources, existing tests automatically outrank written policy, a lone guide is declared comprehensive, or conflicts are erased during synthesis
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: do not alter corpus classifications without evidence and ownership review; observations from a target repository apply to that repository, not automatically to the archived policy
- **revision_decision:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define canonical, supporting, legacy, duplicate, conflicting, and repository-corroboration roles with conflict and promotion procedures
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a single-source hierarchy can still be rigorous when it refuses counterfeit corroboration and uses executable repository behavior to test applicability rather than to multiply authority
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to treat the archived testing-and-fixtures guide as the canonical theme policy, current build files and neighboring tests as implementation corroboration, legacy helpers as compatibility evidence, and conflicting local behavior as a review trigger rather than silently choosing one
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because authority, recency, and executability are different properties; a running legacy test may be current but still encode an obsolete policy, while a canonical guide may be authoritative but intentionally generic
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; generated references are counted as new canonical sources, existing tests automatically outrank written policy, a lone guide is declared comprehensive, or conflicts are erased during synthesis
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: do not alter corpus classifications without evidence and ownership review; observations from a target repository apply to that repository, not automatically to the archived policy
- **revision_decision:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: define canonical, supporting, legacy, duplicate, conflicting, and repository-corroboration roles with conflict and promotion procedures
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies a single-source hierarchy can still be rigorous when it refuses counterfeit corroboration and uses executable repository behavior to test applicability rather than to multiply authority

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: generated references are counted as new canonical sources, existing tests automatically outrank written policy, a lone guide is declared comprehensive, or conflicts are erased during synthesis

## Section 013: Theme Specific Artifact
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed names a fixture plan covering unit, integration, negative, and flaky-test handling, but its three generic fields do not yet make data ownership, lifecycle, realism, determinism, and failure injection reviewable
- **supporting_reason:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because fixtures are hidden test architecture; without explicit lifecycle and fidelity decisions they can leak state, erase production semantics, or make failures irreproducible
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the artifact is a list of test filenames, one fixture serves incompatible boundaries, random data lacks a seed, cleanup depends on test order, or flaky handling consists of retries without diagnosis
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: require artifact depth proportional to risk and reuse; do not impose heavyweight builders on trivial values or reuse infrastructure without proven isolation
- **revision_decision:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to expand the three seed fields into a reviewable fixture-plan schema with lifecycle, fidelity, failure injection, deterministic replay, cleanup, and flake-diagnosis rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the fixture plan is also a concurrency and ownership design; making lifecycle explicit often reveals production ambiguities such as transaction scope, clock ownership, and idempotency keys before implementation

## Section 015: Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed gives one lead-time indicator, one guessed-behavior signal, and a refresh cadence, but those measures cannot reveal whether fixtures catch faults, remain deterministic, or cost more than their evidence is worth
- **supporting_reason:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because speed, stability, and detection power can move in opposite directions, so one lead-time metric invites optimization that weakens semantic coverage
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: coverage percentage becomes the outcome, retries erase first-run failures, suite duration is improved by removing realistic tests without replacing evidence, or arbitrary universal thresholds are presented as service objectives
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: do not compare unrelated repositories, do not infer causation from a single trend, and do not claim a quantitative improvement without retained baseline and measurement method

## Section 016: Completeness Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed checks scenario, tradeoffs, hierarchy, artifact, examples, metrics, and routing, but it does not test whether the fixture plan actually covers the requirement's positive, negative, concurrency, lifecycle, and evidence obligations
- **supporting_reason:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a checklist prevents omission only when its entries are observable and cannot all be satisfied by the same generic paragraph
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: items are self-attested, a passing happy path satisfies multiple distinct risks, not-applicable entries lack reasons, or document completeness is mistaken for backend correctness
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: scale checklist depth to the requirement while preserving mandatory evidence boundaries, command honesty, and explicit not-applicable reasoning
- **revision_decision:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain all seven inherited checks and add evidence locators, behavior coverage, fixture lifecycle, deterministic execution, Red proof, and cold-reader acceptance
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that checklist quality can be tested by evidence locality: when proof is hard to locate, the plan is not yet an effective handoff even if the tests themselves pass
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because a checklist prevents omission only when its entries are observable and cannot all be satisfied by the same generic paragraph

## Section 017: Adjacent Reference Routing
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed suggests generic Kotlin, backend, and testing neighbors but does not name the decision signal that should move a reader away from fixture design or define what evidence accompanies the handoff
- **supporting_reason:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because routing by unresolved decision preserves context and avoids asking a testing guide to decide transactions, framework migration, production capacity, or authorization policy beyond its evidence
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: routing is keyword-based, sends every coroutine question away, drops prior evidence, creates a loop among generic references, or uses an adjacent file to avoid writing the necessary test
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: do not open or rewrite an adjacent assignment while the current file remains incomplete; routing guidance describes downstream use, not permission to violate sequential ownership
- **revision_decision:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace generic neighbor suggestions with decision-based routes, handoff payloads, loop prevention, and return criteria
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that good routing is reversible: it narrows one uncertainty, returns a concrete decision, and leaves a trace showing why fixture scope changed

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed frames a service operating workload with one boundary, up to 25 endpoints or workers, 1000 representative requests, and one rollback path, but it does not translate those inherited planning bounds into test-suite topology or fixture demand
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because fixture architecture that works for one serial route test can leak data, saturate containers, or lose diagnostic precision when multiplied across endpoints, workers, and concurrent requests
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the inherited 25 and 1000 values are treated as universal capacity guarantees, request volume substitutes for behavior diversity, shared state becomes unbounded, or one enormous matrix obscures separate ownership boundaries

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed defines four strong reference-quality thresholds, including 100 percent evidence labels, 18 of 20 correct routing decisions, zero unsupported claims, and recovery paths for every avoid case, but it does not define samples or connect them to fixture reliability
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because source hygiene can make advice auditable while the resulting suite still flakes or misses defects; conversely, a stable test can support an unsupported claim
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: 100 percent is claimed without enumerating recommendations, 18 of 20 uses are cherry-picked, zero unsupported claims is confused with zero uncertainty, or rerun success hides first-run instability
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: preserve the inherited thresholds as this artifact's acceptance policy without generalizing them to product availability, defect rates, or statistical guarantees
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define denominators and failure actions for all seed targets, then add separately calibrated fixture stability and fault-detection evidence
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that reliability has two orthogonal axes: epistemic reliability of the guidance and operational reliability of the tests; both must pass before a strong backend claim is warranted

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed lists source drift, generic advice, request surge, and security-boundary failure, yet it does not show how a fixture suite reveals, masks, or recovers from those failures

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed defines bounded source-refresh retries and generation backpressure, but testing fixtures also need to distinguish a legitimate product retry scenario from a test rerun that conceals nondeterminism
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because unclassified reruns destroy diagnostic evidence and can turn probabilistic success into a false green while additional work increases queue and context pressure
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: CI retries until success, product retry policy is tested by rerunning the test process, containers are recreated without examining leaked state, or agents continue generating sections after normalized uniqueness or heading checks fail
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: never use retries to meet a pass-rate target, never discard first-failure evidence, and separate test-process reruns from application-level retry semantics
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to extend the inherited source workflow with a failure taxonomy, hypothesis-bound reruns, flake quarantine controls, and explicit stop signals for fixture gates
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that backpressure protects epistemic quality as much as compute capacity: stopping preserves the causal chain needed to distinguish a flaky harness from a flaky product
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to classify the failure first as product defect, assertion defect, fixture leak, scheduling nondeterminism, unavailable dependency, stale evidence, or true contradiction; rerun only to test a named hypothesis and preserve the first result
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because unclassified reruns destroy diagnostic evidence and can turn probabilistic success into a false green while additional work increases queue and context pressure
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; CI retries until success, product retry policy is tested by rerunning the test process, containers are recreated without examining leaked state, or agents continue generating sections after normalized uniqueness or heading checks fail
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: never use retries to meet a pass-rate target, never discard first-failure evidence, and separate test-process reruns from application-level retry semantics
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: extend the inherited source workflow with a failure taxonomy, hypothesis-bound reruns, flake quarantine controls, and explicit stop signals for fixture gates
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies backpressure protects epistemic quality as much as compute capacity: stopping preserves the causal chain needed to distinguish a flaky harness from a flaky product
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: the retry has a bounded count, controlled variable, retained seed or trace, expected discriminating outcome, and escalation path; new implementation pauses when core gates are red
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because unclassified reruns destroy diagnostic evidence and can turn probabilistic success into a false green while additional work increases queue and context pressure

- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in the retry has a bounded count, controlled variable, retained seed or trace, expected discriminating outcome, and escalation path; new implementation pauses when core gates are red

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: CI retries until success, product retry policy is tested by rerunning the test process, containers are recreated without examining leaked state, or agents continue generating sections after normalized uniqueness or heading checks fail
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are retry annotations masking flakes, cleanup on failure not executing, exponential backoff making tests slow, virtual-time advancement skipping cancellation checks, and shared external rate limits coupling parallel suites

- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: replay with a recorded seed, run serially to test interference, isolate a dependency, inspect virtual time, quarantine with owner and expiry, narrow source scope, or stop for human/infrastructure resolution

- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: extend the inherited source workflow with a failure taxonomy, hypothesis-bound reruns, flake quarantine controls, and explicit stop signals for fixture gates
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: replay with a recorded seed, run serially to test interference, isolate a dependency, inspect virtual time, quarantine with owner and expiry, narrow source scope, or stop for human/infrastructure resolution This changes how the section resolves when to retry evidence collection or a test action, when to stop new work, and how to prevent fixture or infrastructure instability from consuming the workflow.

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed asks for sources, proof commands, latency percentiles, errors, retries, saturation, rollback triggers, and compact journal evidence, but it does not separate product telemetry from test-harness diagnostics or protect sensitive fixture data
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a red or green result without execution context cannot establish causality, especially under concurrency, virtual time, container reuse, or external simulators
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: raw transcript dumps replace summaries, product and harness errors share one counter, retries overwrite the first result, production telemetry is required for local proof, or fixture payloads leak credentials and personal data
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: collect the minimum evidence needed for diagnosis, never expose secrets or real customer data, and do not demand production telemetry for boundaries proven deterministically in process
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to split inherited observations into product, harness, fixture-lifecycle, replay, privacy, and concise handoff evidence

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed requires a service-specific SLO and supplies p95 under 200 ms and p99 under 500 ms only as an absent-SLO fallback, but it mixes handler latency, reference lead time, and documentation review measures without a test-fixture measurement design
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because fixture overhead and harness topology can dominate measurements, while a fast in-process test host may omit the network, database, or serialization cost named by the production claim
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: one unit test duration is called endpoint latency, testApplication results are generalized to network performance, the inherited 200/500 millisecond fallback is treated as a benchmark, or wall-clock sleeps contaminate coroutine timing
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: preserve p95 under 200 ms and p99 under 500 ms as inherited local fallback guidance only, explicitly document when latency does not apply, and never claim measured performance from prose
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to separate product latency, harness overhead, suite feedback, and reviewer time while adding reproducibility, percentile, saturation, and invalidation controls
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that performance fixtures are experimental apparatus; validating their overhead and omitted boundaries is part of validating the claim, not optional test plumbing

- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the deeper deduction is that performance fixtures are experimental apparatus; validating their overhead and omitted boundaries is part of validating the claim, not optional test plumbing

- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: document that latency is not applicable, run a microbenchmark for a pure hot path, use an approved service load harness, measure only suite feedback cost, or defer the performance claim to production-like infrastructure This changes how the section resolves how to verify runtime or suite performance claims without turning inherited fallback numbers into universal Kotlin backend guarantees.

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed stops the reference at multiple systems, ownership boundaries, unbounded discovery, or production traffic without an SLO, but it does not state how to partition fixtures, infrastructure, and verification ownership once that boundary is crossed
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because shared fixture abstractions across independent systems create hidden coupling, while fully isolated plans can leave cross-system contracts untested unless a deliberate integration owner remains
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: parallel agents edit the same artifact, every module invents incompatible fixtures, a monolithic environment serializes all work, or splitting removes responsibility for migration order and cross-service idempotency
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: do not use this single reference as the complete plan for cross-system production traffic or multiple independent owners; preserve one verification owner per split and a named integration owner
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add split criteria, ownership contracts, shared-utility limits, cross-split evidence, CI isolation, and merge-time verification to the retained boundary statements
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that fixture architecture often reveals organizational architecture: cleanup, credentials, and contract ownership make hidden service coupling visible before production deployment
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: do not use this single reference as the complete plan for cross-system production traffic or multiple independent owners; preserve one verification owner per split and a named integration owner

- **supporting_reason:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because targeted retrieval reduces irrelevant tutorials and makes it possible to record the exact claim, version, locator, and invalidation condition
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: queries are run routinely without a stale claim, generic result ranking determines authority, example repositories substitute for framework contracts, or search output is copied into policy without version matching

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 08 on verification method: verification cannot erase the judgment that no query was executed in this no-browse pass, so future result quality, current APIs, and release state remain unknown
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 08 on verification method: reject evidence gathered outside this boundary: do not browse during this assignment, do not infer current facts from query wording, and do not allow public results to override repository behavior without explaining the conflict
- **revision_decision:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 08 on verification method: add pass/fail observations tied to the revision retain the broad seed phrases while adding claim-triggered, versioned query templates and a complete retrieval-to-local-proof record

- **current_section_observation:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the deeper deduction is that a refresh query is a maintenance control rather than evidence itself; its value is measured by whether it resolves one uncertainty and changes or confirms a locally tested decision
- **supporting_reason:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 10 on second-order deductions: that deduction follows from targeted retrieval reduces irrelevant tutorials and makes it possible to record the exact claim, version, locator, and invalidation condition
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where queries are run routinely without a stale claim, generic result ranking determines authority, example repositories substitute for framework contracts, or search output is copied into policy without version matching
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 10 on second-order deductions: carry the deduction forward only within do not browse during this assignment, do not infer current facts from query wording, and do not allow public results to override repository behavior without explaining the conflict

- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: inspect locally cached docs or dependency source, use build metadata and existing tests, preserve uncertainty, ask a maintainer, or defer the recommendation until primary evidence can be retrieved This changes how the section resolves which future retrieval query should be run for a named stale or uncertain testing claim and what evidence must return from it.

## Section 026: Evidence Boundary Notes
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed defines local, external, and combined-inference labels, but it does not show how repository observations, executable test results, stale pointers, and contradictory evidence should be represented
- **supporting_reason:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because testing recommendations often blend policy, framework semantics, local convention, and observed behavior; collapsing them into one authoritative voice hides which part can survive dependency or repository change
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a URL is labeled an external fact without retrieval, passing local behavior is generalized to all Kotlin services, inference is phrased as source quotation, or conflicting results are silently reconciled
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: do not upgrade confidence through repetition, preserve disagreement until a discriminating check exists, and scope executable evidence to the exact environment and versions observed
- **revision_decision:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to extend the three retained labels with retrieval state, repository observation, executable result, conflict handling, confidence criteria, and invalidation metadata
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that evidence labels are control-flow for future maintenance: they tell the next agent whether to reread local policy, refresh a public fact, rerun a test, or reconsider an inference
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to label direct archived local guidance, refreshed external facts, unrefreshed external pointers, target-repository observations, executable results, and combined inference separately, then attach locator, date or version, scope, and invalidation condition
- **supporting_reason:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because testing recommendations often blend policy, framework semantics, local convention, and observed behavior; collapsing them into one authoritative voice hides which part can survive dependency or repository change
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; a URL is labeled an external fact without retrieval, passing local behavior is generalized to all Kotlin services, inference is phrased as source quotation, or conflicting results are silently reconciled
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: do not upgrade confidence through repetition, preserve disagreement until a discriminating check exists, and scope executable evidence to the exact environment and versions observed
- **revision_decision:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: extend the three retained labels with retrieval state, repository observation, executable result, conflict handling, confidence criteria, and invalidation metadata
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies evidence labels are control-flow for future maintenance: they tell the next agent whether to reread local policy, refresh a public fact, rerun a test, or reconsider an inference

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: a URL is labeled an external fact without retrieval, passing local behavior is generalized to all Kotlin services, inference is phrased as source quotation, or conflicting results are silently reconciled

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where a reviewer can trace a claim to its source or command, see whether external content was actually retrieved, identify the inference step, and know what new evidence would reverse it
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 04 on failure boundary: distinguish a genuine failure from an out-of-scope case using do not upgrade confidence through repetition, preserve disagreement until a discriminating check exists, and scope executable evidence to the exact environment and versions observed
- **revision_decision:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: downgrade to provisional guidance, present competing interpretations, run a discriminating local test, request current primary evidence, or leave the decision unresolved with a named owner
